The New-York Sumner Meeting at the South.
NEW-YORK CITY.; Vacant Offices--Office-holders Wanted. Colored Sympathy Meeting. The colored citizens of this City held a meeting last night in Soiloh Presbeterian Church, Prince street, to express sympathy in the case of Mrs. BOOBMAN, a colored lady who, some time ago, having been brought to this State by her master, became free in virtue of the laws of this State; but who, having been called to the aid of her sick husband at Washington, went thither with her children, and on their way through Virginia were captured and ?? in the slave prison. Rev. U.B. RAY repeated the story of Rev. H. W. BEECHER and his girl "SHAH", and claimed kindred aid for the Boorman family. Rev. Mr. GARNET, of Jamaica, W. I., presented the claims of Mrs BOORMAN and family upon the colored people of New-York, in a very effective manner. Revs. Mr. PORTER, Mr. SPELMAN and Mr. PETERSON were present and took part in the proceedings of the meeting. About one hundred and fifty persons, mostly Indias, were present. A Yacht Race. Colored Sympathy Meeting.

LONG ISLAND.
Passengers Arrived.
The Value of Five Dollors. From the Merchants' Magazine. A Man, named PORTER, says be once had a clerical friend, between whom and himself there existed great intimacy. Every Saturday night, as PORTER was sitting balancing his cash, a note would come requesting "the loan of a five dollar bill." The money was always returned punctually at 8 o'clock on the Monday morning. But what puzzled the lender was, the Parson always returned the very identical note he borrowed.

NEW-YORK CITY.; Mercantile Library--annual Election. The annual election of Officers of the Mere. Extension of Sixth-Avenue. Thirteenth Ward Repubilcan Association. The annual election of Officers of the Mercantile Library Association took place last evening, at Clinton Hall. There was a large gathering of the members, and the juvenile portion, while the Inspectors were counting the votes, enjoyed themselves in a questionable manner in the Lectureroom. Their principal amusement was the destruction of the hats of their fellows by a free use of the cushions. But as there was no ill-humor, it was perhaps well enough to let the little boys have a good time. Soft Soap vs. Hardware. Aid for the Cape de Verde Islanders. Changing the Name of Chatham-street and Park-row. sale of a Valuable Library. Parade and Review of the Military. The Turf for 1856. Concerning the Oliver-street Marriage. Morrisania Sabbath Schools. NEW-YORK CITY.; Spiritualism Exposed. A tolerably run audience was drawn on Monday night to the Tabernacle, by Professor SPENCER'S announcement of his intention then and 'there to expose all the so-called phenomena of modern spiritualism. He prefaced his experiments by a semi-explanatory, and semi-declamatory address, opening with the profound and original remark, "Truth is immortal and can never die." Strawberries. SUPERIOR COURT- COURT CALENDAR-- Decision in Equity. Decisions in Admiralty. The Enlistment Cases--Nollo Prosequal. SUPERIOR COURT- SUPERIOR COURT--SPECIAL TERM--March, 1856. ?? TION FOR INJUNCTION--IMPORTANT DECISION SUSTAINING THE RIGHTS OF MERCHANTS AND MANUFACTURERS TO THEIR TRADE-MARKS AND LABELS. India Rubber Comb Company vs. William Taster.-- ?? was an action brought by the plaintiff to restrain the ??fendast from using the plainftiff's trade-marks and bels, or fraudulent or simulated resemblances and imitions of the same. On filing the complaint, an order on Court was obtained, requiring the defendant to show use why an injuction should not be issued, forbidding as then using them, and tempararily restraining him ?? such use. The defendant put in an answer, and produced many affidavits in support of the course pursuent him, and seeking to justify it a

Grand Republican Demonstration at Boston. BOSTON, Sunday, Oct. 26. An immense Republican meeting was held at the National Theatre last evening, Hon. JOSIAH QUINCY presiding. Hon. A. BURLINGAME was the first speaker. He spoke for two hours, advocating the claims of the National Republicans to the united support of the friends of freedom, and concluded by stating that he would reserve for another occasion a personal statement. He was followed by Hon. N. P. BANKS, whose address was mainly confined to local

LATEST INTELLIGENCE; By Telegraph to the New-York Daily Times. XXXIVth CONGRESS----First Session. HOUSE OF REPRESENTATIVES.
The Ten Governors. The Board of Almshouse Governors, not to be outdone by- Congress or the Legislature, has hesitated ever since the new Board came together,- in regard to the choice of President, and only settled its troubles on Saturday night. Meetings were held on Wednesday and Thursday, and a third on Saturday finished the business. The number of the Governors who braved the furious storm to do their duty was just enough to elect, but there was no spice, and on the fourteenth and last ballot the result was as follows: Simeon Draper.......... Blank ..................1
